# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Django ORM Raw SQL Injection Prevention

## Your Task

Find all Python source files in django/django that handle raw SQL queries and prevent SQL injection: the RawSQL expression sanitization, the raw() queryset method parameter binding, and the cursor.execute() parameterization enforcement.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the security domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/django--674eda1c.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/django--674eda1c` (django/django)

Perfect! I've created a comprehensive `answer.json` file documenting all the Python source files in django/django that handle raw SQL queries and prevent SQL injection. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Summary

The answer includes **16 files** across django/django that implement SQL injection prevention for raw SQL queries:

### Key Files Identified:

**Core Django ORM Files:**
- `django/db/models/expressions.py` - RawSQL class and expression sanitization
- `django/db/models/query.py` - raw() and extra() methods, RawQuerySet class
- `django/db/models/sql/query.py` - RawQuery class and execution logic

**Database Backend Files:**
- `django/db/backends/utils.py` - CursorWrapper with execute() and parameter passing
- `django/db/backends/base/operations.py` - adapt_unknown_value() for type conversion
- `django/db/backends/base/base.py` - Transaction validation
- Backend-specific files (MySQL, PostgreSQL, Oracle, SQLite)

**Documentation Files:**
- `docs/topics/db/sql.txt` - Raw SQL best practices
- `docs/topics/security.txt` - SQL injection protection documentation
- `docs/ref/models/expressions.txt` - RawSQL expression documentation

### Four-Layer Protection Mechanism:

1. **RawSQL Expressions** - Keep SQL and params separate
2. **raw() Method** - Creates RawQuerySet with parameter binding
3. **extra() Method** - Allows SQL fragments with param safety
4. **cursor.execute() Enforcement** - Database driver parameterization

The key insight is that Django **never interpolates user input into SQL strings**. Instead, parameters are always passed separately to the database driver, which handles escaping safely through parameterized queries.

This can result in records\\n99: being deleted or data leakage.\\n100: \\n101: Django's querysets are protected from SQL injection since their queries are\\n102: constructed using query parameterization. A query's SQL code is defined\\n103: separately from the query's parameters. Parameters are adapted for each backend type (MySQL, PostgreSQL, Oracle, SQLite) using backend-specific methods\\n4. Documentation in `docs/topics/db/sql.txt` and `docs/topics/security.txt` emphasizes that placeholders must NOT be quoted and params must be used\\n5. The `validate_no_broken_transaction()` call in `_execute()` ensures transaction integrity during parameter binding\\n\\nThis three-layer approach prevents SQL injection by ensuring parameters are never directly interpolated into SQL strings and are instead handled by the database driver's parameterization mechanism, which safely escapes all user input.\"\n}\n",

  "new_string": "  \"text\": \"Django's SQL injection prevention for raw SQL queries involves multiple layers of protection across four main mechanisms:\\n\\n## 1. RawSQL Expression Sanitization\\n\\nThe `RawSQL` class in `django/db/models/expressions.py` (lines 1236-1268) represents raw SQL expressions used within query annotations. It stores both the SQL template and parameters separately:\\n- Constructor (line 1239) accepts `sql`, `params`, and optional `output_field`\\n- The `as_sql()` method (lines 1248-1249) returns the SQL wrapped in parentheses along with the params tuple: `return \\\"(%s)\\\" % self.sql, self.params`\\n- Parameters are never interpolated into the SQL string directly; they remain separate for database driver parameterization\\n- The `resolve_expression()` method (lines 1254-1268) handles field resolution for parent class fields referenced in raw SQL\\n\\n## 2. raw() QuerySet Method Parameter Binding\\n\\nThe `raw()` method in `django/db/models/query.py` (lines 1461-1473) creates a `RawQuerySet` instance that handles raw SQL queries returning model instances:\\n- Accepts `raw_query`, `params=()`, `translations=None`, and `using=None`\\n- Creates a `RawQuerySet` object that stores both the SQL query and parameters separately\\n- The `RawQuerySet` class (lines 2210-2237) initializes with the raw query and params, creating an internal `RawQuery` object (line 2231): `self.query = query or sql.RawQuery(sql=raw_query, using=self.db, params=params)`\\n\\n## 3. extra() QuerySet Method for SQL Fragments\\n\\nThe `extra()` method in `django/db/models/query.py` (lines 1876-1891) allows developers to add raw SQL fragments while maintaining parameter safety:\\n- Accepts `select`, `where`, `params`, `tables`, `order_by`, and `select_params` arguments\\n- Delegates to `clone.query.add_extra()` which maintains separate parameter lists for different SQL fragments\\n- The `params` argument ensures WHERE clause parameters are properly bound\\n- The `select_params` argument ensures SELECT clause parameters are properly bound\\n- Both `where` and `select` fragments use `%s` placeholders that are filled via parameter binding, not string interpolation\\n\\n## 4. cursor.execute() Parameterization Enforcement\\n\\nThe core parameter binding enforcement happens through several interconnected components:\\n\\n**RawQuery Execution (django/db/models/sql/query.py, lines 150-220)**:\\n- The `RawQuery._execute_query()` method (lines 203-220) handles the actual execution\\n- It adapts parameters using `connection.ops.adapt_unknown_value()` (lines 209-217) to convert Python types to database-safe values\\n- Type handling for tuple and dict parameters ensures proper escaping based on parameter type (lines 210-217)\\n- The method calls `self.cursor.execute(self.sql, params)` (line 220) with SQL and params separate\\n\\n**CursorWrapper Parameter Handling (django/db/backends/utils.py, lines 17-150)**:\\n- The `CursorWrapper.execute()` method (lines 78-81) delegates to `_execute_with_wrappers()` which passes params separately\\n- The `_execute_with_wrappers()` method (lines 88-92) allows execution wrappers to intercept calls while preserving parameter separation\\n- The `_execute()` method (lines 94-105) validates database state with `validate_no_broken_transaction()` (line 99) and passes params to the actual cursor\\n- If params is None, it calls cursor.execute(sql) without params; otherwise, calls cursor.execute(sql, params) (lines 101-105)\\n- This enforces that parameters are always passed via the database driver's parameter binding mechanism\\n\\n**Parameter Adaptation (django/db/backends/base/operations.py, lines 550-600)**:\\n- The `adapt_unknown_value()` method (lines 550-567) provides type conversion for raw SQL query parameters\\n- Handles datetime, date, time, and decimal conversions before passing to the database (lines 558-567)\\n- These conversions ensure proper escaping while maintaining type safety\\n\\n**Backend-Specific Parameter Handling**:\\n- Each database backend (MySQL, PostgreSQL, Oracle, SQLite) has specific cursor classes that handle parameter conversion\\n- For example, PostgreSQL's `mogrify()` function in `django/db/backends/postgresql/operations.py` (line 195) converts parameters for debugging\\n- Oracle's `_param_generator()` method in `django/db/backends/oracle/base.py` handles Oracle-specific parameter binding\\n\\n**Field-Level Parameter Preparation (django/db/models/fields/__init__.py)**:\\n- Methods like `get_db_prep_value()` and `get_db_prep_save()` ensure field values are properly prepared for database operations\\n- These are called during expression compilation to handle parameter values in ORM queries\\n- While not directly in raw SQL paths, they establish the pattern for parameter preparation\\n\\n**Documentation and Security Enforcement (docs/topics/)**:\\n- `docs/topics/db/sql.txt` (lines 29-35, 262-267) emphasizes that placeholders must NOT be quoted and params must be used\\n- `docs/topics/security.txt` (lines 91-112) defines SQL injection protection strategy and warns about raw SQL methods\\n- `docs/ref/models/expressions.txt` (lines 802-828) documents RawSQL parameters requirement\\n\\n**Security Key Points**:\\n1. SQL and parameters are ALWAYS kept separate throughout the execution chain\\n2. The database driver's native parameter binding (not Django string interpolation) is used\\n3. Parameters are adapted for each backend type using backend-specific methods in `adapt_unknown_value()`\\n4. Unquoted placeholders (`%s`, not `'%s'`) must be used to prevent SQL injection\\n5. The `validate_no_broken_transaction()` call in `_execute()` ensures transaction integrity during parameter binding\\n6. Both `raw()` and `extra()` methods support `params` arguments for safe parameter binding\\n7. When parameters are not provided via params argument, they are adapted from their Python types\\n\\nThis four-layer approach (RawSQL expressions, raw() method, extra() method, and cursor.execute() enforcement) prevents SQL injection by ensuring parameters are never directly interpolated into SQL strings and are instead handled by the database driver's parameterization mechanism, which safely escapes all user input.\"",

When parameters are not provided via params argument, they are adapted from their Python types\\n\\nThis four-layer approach (RawSQL expressions, raw() method, extra() method, and cursor.execute() enforcement) prevents SQL injection by ensuring parameters are never directly interpolated into SQL strings and are instead handled by the database driver's parameterization mechanism, which safely escapes all user input.\"\n}\n",
